Run `openclaw gateway install`\\n4. Run `openclaw gateway status` or `openclaw doctor`\\n\\n**Expected behavior**\\n\\nThe Scheduled Task is properly configured with:\\n- Program/script: `C:\\\\Users\\\\\\\\.openclaw\\\\gateway.cmd`\\n- Arguments: (empty or `gateway`)\\n- Start in: `C:\\\\Users\\\\\\\\.openclaw\\\\`\\n\\n**Actual behavior**\\n\\n`openclaw gateway status` reports:\\n```\\nService config issue: Service command does not include the gateway subcommand\\nCommand: setlocal enabledelayedexpansion\\nService file: C:\\\\Users\\\\\\\\.openclaw\\\\gateway.cmd\\n```\\n\\n`schtasks /query /tn \\u0026#34;OpenClaw Gateway\\u0026#34; /fo LIST /v` shows:\\n- **Program/script**: Contains the entire raw content of `gateway.cmd` starting with `setlocal enabledelayedexpansion` (the batch file content itself, not a path)\\n- **Start in**: blank/N/A\\n\\nThis means the Scheduled Task is executing the batch file content as a command string, rather than executing the `.cmd` file as a script.\\n\\n**Root cause**\\n\\n1. The `schtasks` command used during `openclaw gateway install` may not properly escape or handle the username path when specifying the batch file path in the Program field.\\n2. The `SCRIPT` variable inside `gateway.cmd` is hardcoded to a path that may differ from the actual user path due to character-level differences in the username (e.g., Unicode apostrophe vs ASCII apostrophe).\\n3. Routing local services through a public proxy — adds unnecessary latency and defeats the purpose of self-hosting.\\n\\n### Impact\\n\\n- **Affected:** Teams running self-hosted search engines (SearXNG, etc.) or air-gapped/private deployments\\n- **Severity:** Blocks workflow — private network access is completely unavailable today\\n- **Frequency:** Always, for any private-network deployment\\n- **Consequence:** Self-hosted search is non-functional; operators must use cloud search providers even when a local alternative exists\\n\\n### Evidence/examples\\n\\n- SearXNG Docker setup requires access to `127.x.x.x` or `192.168.x.x` by default\\n- Comparable `allowPrivateNetwork` patterns exist in Fetch API specs and other gateway frameworks\\n- Schema validation for the new flag is covered in `src/config/zod-schema.agent-runtime.ts`\\n- New search providers (Tavily, SearXNG) added alongside this change\\n\\n### Additional information\\n\\n- Must remain backward-compatible: `allowPrivateNetwork` defaults to `false`, preserving existing SSRF protection for all non-local deployments\\n- A troubleshooting guide for plaintext WebSocket/HTTP issues on private networks is included in `docs/websearch.md`\\n- No sensitive credentials or private configuration data are exposed by this change\",\"state\":\"OPEN\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"leemgs\"},\"labels\":[\"enhancement\"],\"created_at\":\"2026-03-24T06:34:25Z\",\"updated_at\":\"2026-03-24T06:34:25Z\"}],\"totalCount\":9063,\"pageInfo\":{\"hasNextPage\":true,\"hasPreviousPage\":false,\"startCursor\":\"Y3Vyc29yOnYyOpK5MjAyNi0wMy0yM1QyMzo0NjoyNi0wNzowMM716Imf\",\"endCursor\":\"Y3Vyc29yOnYyOpK5MjAyNi0wMy0yM1QyMzozNDoyNS0wNzowMM7158nI\"}}"}]}

macOS/Linux that seems natural.\\nOn Windows, cron+exec feels unreliable because:\\n\\ncommands are rewritten with cd ~\\\\clawd...,\\nexec host not allowed sometimes blocks host execution,\\nand That snapshot can be stale relative to disk.\\n\\nThis means a normal gateway-side auth write like usage/cooldown/last-good persistence can do this:\\n\\n1. CLI / Configure / Onboard writes a fresh credential to `auth-profiles.json`\\n2. gateway later acquires the auth-store file lock\\n3. locked write reloads the stale in-memory runtime snapshot instead of disk\\n4. gateway saves that stale snapshot back to disk\\n5. fresh token/order/config appears to \\\"revert\\\"\\n\\nThis is the same class of bug as #45516, but it also affects actual credential replacement instead of only auth order.\\n\\n## Repro shape\\n\\n- Have a running gateway with an old OpenAI token loaded in memory\\n- Save a fresh OpenAI token via Configure / Onboard\\n- Trigger any gateway-side auth-store write (`markAuthProfileUsed`, cooldown/failure persistence, `lastGood` updates, etc.)\\n- `auth-profiles.json` can be rewritten with the stale token from runtime memory\\n\\n## Expected\\n\\nLocked auth-store writers should reload from disk under the file lock, not from the runtime snapshot.\\n\\n## Scope\\n\\nThis can affect:\\n\\n- Configure / Onboard token fresh token save can revert to stale expired profile under live gateway\",\"body\":\"## Bug\\n\\nSaving a fresh OpenAI token through Configure or Onboard can appear to work, then revert back to a stale expired token while the gateway is still running.\\n\\nRelated: #45516\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nLocked auth-profile writes in `src/agents/auth-profiles/store.ts` reload from `ensureAuthProfileStore(...)`, which prefers the runtime auth-store snapshot when one exists. That snapshot can be stale relative to disk.\\n\\nThis means a normal gateway-side auth write like usage/cooldown/last-good persistence can do this:\\n\\n1. CLI / Configure / Onboard writes a fresh credential to `auth-profiles.json`\\n2. gateway later acquires the auth-store file lock\\n3. locked write reloads the stale in-memory runtime snapshot instead of disk\\n4. gateway saves that stale snapshot back to disk\\n5. fresh token/order/config appears to \\\"revert\\\"\\n\\nThis is the same class of bug as #45516, but it also affects actual credential replacement instead of only auth order.\\n\\n## Repro shape\\n\\n- Have a running gateway with an old OpenAI token loaded in memory\\n- Save a fresh OpenAI token via Configure / Onboard\\n- Trigger any gateway-side auth-store write (`markAuthProfileUsed`, cooldown/failure persistence, `lastGood` updates, etc.)\\n- `auth-profiles.json` can be rewritten with the stale token from runtime memory\\n\\n## Expected\\n\\nLocked auth-store writers should reload from disk under the file lock, not from the runtime snapshot.\\n\\n## Scope\\n\\nThis can affect:\\n\\n- Configure / Onboard token replacement\\n- `models auth order set`\\n- any other fresh auth-profile change that races a later gateway-side auth store {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01WrmhiLYSa1M5syMdTeep51","type":"tool_result","content":[{"type":"text","text":"{\"total_count\":3764,\"incomplete_results\":false,\"items\":[{\"id\":3998933935,\"number\":28259,\"state\":\"open\",\"locked\":false,\"title\":\"Plugin lifecycle hooks: onInstall/onUpdate for setup scripts\",\"body\":\"## Problem\\n\\nPlugins that need to install external dependencies (e.g. a Python CLI via `uv`) currently rely on npm `postinstall` in package.json. This is blocked by OpenClaw's security sandbox, so the script never runs on install or update.\\n\\nThere's no fallback mechanism — plugins have no lifecycle hook to run setup with appropriate permissions.\\n\\n## Real-World Impact\\n\\nThe `@basicmemory/openclaw-basic-memory` plugin needs to install the `bm` CLI via `uv tool install`. After plugin install/update, the bundled `postinstall` is silently blocked. Users have to manually run `bash scripts/setup-bm.sh` to get the right version. When the CLI is outdated, the plugin's MCP connection fails in a retry loop (every tool call gates on a startup check that never passes).\\n\\n## Proposed Solution\\n\\nAdd plugin lifecycle hooks that run with appropriate permissions:\\n\\n- **`onInstall`** — runs once after first install\\n- **`onUpdate`** — runs after plugin version changes\\n- **`onStartup`** (optional) — runs on gateway start, for plugins that need to verify their environment\\n\\nThese could be declared in `openclaw.plugin.json` and executed by the gateway with user-level (not sandboxed) permissions, possibly with an approval prompt on first run.\\n\\n## References\\n\\n- basicmachines-co/openclaw-basic-memory#25 — plugin-side workaround lifecycle hooks: onInstall/onUpdate for setup scripts\",\"body\":\"## Problem\\n\\nPlugins that need to install external dependencies (e.g. a Python CLI via `uv`) currently rely on npm `postinstall` in package.json. This is blocked by OpenClaw's security sandbox, so the script never runs on install or update.\\n\\nThere's no fallback mechanism — plugins have no lifecycle hook to run setup with appropriate permissions.\\n\\n## Real-World Impact\\n\\nThe `@basicmemory/openclaw-basic-memory` plugin needs to install the `bm` CLI via `uv tool install`. After plugin install/update, the bundled `postinstall` is silently blocked. Users have to manually run `bash scripts/setup-bm.sh` to get the right version. When the CLI is outdated, the plugin's MCP connection fails in a retry loop (every tool call gates on a startup check that never passes).\\n\\n## Proposed Solution\\n\\nAdd plugin lifecycle hooks that run with appropriate permissions:\\n\\n- **`onInstall`** — runs once after first install\\n- **`onUpdate`** — runs after plugin version changes\\n- **`onStartup`** (optional) — runs on gateway start, for plugins that need to verify their environment\\n\\nThese could be declared in `openclaw.plugin.json` and executed by the gateway with user-level (not sandboxed) permissions, possibly with an approval prompt on first run.\\n\\n## References\\n\\n- basicmachines-co/openclaw-basic-memory#25 — plugin-side workaround
